Company&#146;s primary exposure to movements in foreign currency exchange rates relate to non-U.S. dollar denominated sales in Europe, Japan, Australia, Canada, and certain parts of Asia, as well as non-U.S. dollar denominated operating expenses
incurred throughout the world. Weakening of foreign currencies relative to the U.S. dollar will adversely affect the U.S. dollar value of the Company&#146;s foreign currency-denominated sales and earnings, and generally will lead the Company to
raise international pricing, potentially reducing demand for the Company&#146;s products. In some circumstances, due to competition or other reasons, the Company may decide not to raise local prices to the full extent of the dollar&#146;s
strengthening, or at all, which would adversely affect the U.S. dollar value of the Company&#146;s foreign currency denominated sales and earnings. Conversely, a strengthening of foreign currencies, while generally beneficial to the Company&#146;s
foreign currency-denominated sales and earnings, could cause the Company to reduce international pricing, thereby limiting the benefit. Additionally, strengthening of foreign currencies may also increase the Company&#146;s cost of product components
denominated in those currencies, thus adversely affecting gross margins. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="justify"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">The Company has used derivative instruments, such as foreign
exchange forward and option positions, to hedge certain exposures to fluctuations in foreign currency exchange rates. The use of such hedging activities may not offset any or more than a portion of the adverse financial effects of unfavorable
movements in foreign exchange rates over the limited time the hedges are in place. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><I>The Company&#146;s retail business has required and will continue to
require a substantial investment and commitment of resources and is subject to numerous risks and uncertainties. </I></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="justify"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Through March&nbsp;28,

substantial operating lease commitments for retail space with terms ranging from 5 to 20 years, the majority of which are for 10 years. Certain stores have been designed and built to serve as high-profile venues to promote brand awareness and serve
as vehicles for corporate sales and marketing activities. Because of their unique design elements, locations and size, these stores require substantially more investment than the Company&#146;s more typical retail stores. Due to the high fixed cost
structure associated with the Retail segment, a decline in sales or the closure or poor performance of individual or multiple stores could result in significant lease termination costs, write-offs of equipment and leasehold improvements, and
severance costs that could have a material adverse effect on the Company&#146;s financial condition and operating results. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="justify"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Many factors
unique to retail operations, some of which are beyond the Company&#146;s control, pose risks and uncertainties that could have a material adverse effect on the Retail segment&#146;s future results, cause its actual results to differ from anticipated
results and have a material adverse effect on the Company&#146;s financial condition and operating results. These risks and uncertainties include, among other things, macro-economic factors that could have a negative effect on general retail
activity, as well as the Company&#146;s inability to manage costs associated with store </FONT>
</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></P>

 <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="justify">
<FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">construction and operation, inability to sell third-party products at adequate margins, failure to manage relationships with existing retail channel
partners, more challenging environment in managing retail operations outside the U.S., costs associated with unanticipated fluctuations in the value of retail inventory, and inability to obtain and renew leases in quality retail locations at a
reasonable cost. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="justify"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><I>Investment in new business strategies and initiatives could disrupt the Company&#146;s ongoing business and present
risks not originally contemplated. </I></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="justify"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">The Company has invested, and in the future may invest, in new business strategies or acquisitions.
Such endeavors may involve significant risks and uncertainties, including distraction of management from current operations, insufficient revenue to offset liabilities assumed and expenses associated with the strategy, inadequate return of capital,
and unidentified issues not discovered in the Company&#146;s due diligence. Because these new ventures are inherently risky, no assurance can be given that such strategies and initiatives will be successful and will not have a material adverse
effect on the Company&#146;s financial condition and operating results. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><I>The Company&#146;s future operating performance depends on the performance of
distributors, carriers, and other resellers. </I></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="justify"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">The Company distributes its products through wholesalers, resellers, national and regional
retailers, value-added resellers, and cataloguers, many of whom distribute products from competing manufacturers. The Company also sells many of its products and resells third-party products in most of its major markets directly to end-users,
certain education customers, and certain resellers through its online and retail stores. iPhone is distributed through the Company, its cellular network carriers&#146; distribution channels, and certain third-party resellers. </FONT></P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="justify"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Many resellers operate on narrow product margins and have been negatively affected in the past by weak economic conditions. Some resellers have perceived
the expansion of the Company&#146;s direct sales as conflicting with their business interests as distributors and resellers of the Company&#146;s products. Such a perception could discourage resellers from investing resources in the distribution and
sale of the Company&#146;s products or lead them to limit or cease distribution of those products. The Company&#146;s financial condition and operating results could be materially adversely affected if the financial condition of these resellers
weakens, if resellers stopped distributing the Company&#146;s products, or if uncertainty regarding demand for the Company&#146;s products caused resellers to reduce their ordering and marketing of the Company&#146;s products. The Company has
invested and will continue to invest in programs to enhance reseller sales, including staffing selected resellers&#146; stores with Company employees and contractors and improving product placement displays. These programs could require a
substantial investment while providing no assurance of return or incremental revenue. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><I>The Company is exposed to credit risk and fluctuations in the
market values of its investment portfolio. </I></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="justify"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Although the Company has not recognized any material losses on its cash, cash equivalents
and marketable securities, future declines in their market values could have a material adverse effect on the Company&#146;s financial condition and operating results. Given the global nature of its business, the Company has investments both
domestically and internationally. Additionally, the Company&#146;s overall investment portfolio is often concentrated in the financial sector, which has been negatively impacted by the recent market liquidity conditions. Credit ratings and pricing
of these investments can be negatively impacted by liquidity, credit deterioration or losses, financial results, or other factors. As a result, the value or liquidity of the Company&#146;s cash, cash equivalents and marketable securities could
decline and result in a material impairment, which could have a material adverse effect on the Company&#146;s financial condition and operating results. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="justify"><FONT
FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><I>The Company is exposed to credit risk on its accounts receivable and prepayments related to long-term supply agreements. This risk is heightened during periods when economic conditions worsen. </I></FONT></P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="justify"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">A substantial majority of the Company&#146;s outstanding trade receivables are not covered by collateral or credit insurance. The Company also has
unsecured non-trade receivables resulting from purchases of components by contract manufacturers and other vendors that manufacture sub-assemblies or assemble final products for the </FONT>
</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></P>
 <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="center"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">54 </FONT></P>


<p Style='page-break-before:always'>
<HR  SIZE="3" COLOR="#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">

 <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="justify">
<FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Company. In addition, the Company has made prepayments associated with long-term supply agreements to secure supply of certain inventory components. While
the Company has procedures to monitor and limit exposure to credit risk on its trade and non-trade receivables as well as long-term prepayments, there can be no assurance such procedures will effectively limit its credit risk and avoid losses, which
could have a material adverse effect on the Company&#146;s financial condition and operating results. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><I>The Company is subject to risks associated with
laws and regulations related to health, safety and environmental protection. </I></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="justify"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">The Company&#146;s products and services, and the
production and distribution of those goods and services, are subject to a variety of laws and regulations. These may require the Company to offer customers the ability to return a product at the end of its useful life and place responsibility for
environmentally safe disposal or recycling with the Company. Such laws and regulations have been passed in several jurisdictions in which the Company operates, including various countries within Europe and Asia, certain Canadian provinces and
certain states within the U.S. Although the Company does not anticipate any material adverse effects based on the nature of its operations and the thrust of such laws, there is no assurance such existing laws or future laws will not have a material
adverse effect on the Company&#146;s financial condition and operating results. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><I>Changes in the Company&#146;s tax rates could affect its future
results. </I></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="justify"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">The Company&#146;s future effective tax rates could be affected by changes in the mix of earnings in countries with differing
statutory tax rates, changes in the valuation of deferred tax assets and liabilities, or changes in tax laws or their interpretation. The Company is subject to the continuous examination of its income tax returns by the Internal Revenue Service and
other tax authorities. The Company regularly assesses the likelihood of adverse outcomes resulting from these examinations to determine the adequacy of its provision for taxes. There can be no assurance that the outcomes from these examinations will
not have a material adverse effect on the Company&#146;s financial condition and operating results. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><I>The Company is subject to risks associated with the
availability and coverage of insurance. </I></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="justify"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">For certain risks, the Company does not maintain insurance coverage because of cost and/or
availability.&nbsp;Because the Company retains some portion of its insurable risks, and in some cases self-insures completely, unforeseen or catastrophic losses in excess of insured limits could have a material adverse effect on the Company&#146;s
financial condition and operating results. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="font-size:18px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P>

<TD VALIGN="top"> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="1"><B>Business Conduct</B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman"
SIZE="1"><B>The&nbsp;way&nbsp;we&nbsp;do&nbsp;business worldwide</B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:1px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="1">February 2009</FONT></P></TD>

<TD WIDTH="29%"></TD>
<TD VALIGN="bottom" WIDTH="2%"></TD>
<TD WIDTH="69%"></TD></TR>
<TR>
<TD VALIGN="top"></TD>
<TD VALIGN="bottom"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
<TD VALIGN="bottom"> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="6">Business Conduct</FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="3"><B>The way we do business
worldwide</B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Apple conducts business ethically, honestly, and in full compliance with all laws and regulations. This applies to every business decision in
every area of the company worldwide.</FONT></P> <P STYLE="font-size:24px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="font-size:24px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P> <P
STYLE="font-size:24px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="3">Apple&#146;s Principles of Business Conduct</FONT></P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Apple&#146;s success is based on creating innovative, high-quality products and services and on demonstrating integrity in every business interaction. Apple&#146;s
principles of business conduct define the way we do business worldwide. These principles are:</FONT></P> <P STYLE="font-size:6px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px; margin-left:1.00em; text-indent:-1.00em"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">&#149;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<B>Honesty.</B> Demonstrate honesty and high ethical standards in all business dealings.</FONT></P> <P
STYLE="font-size:6px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px; margin-left:1.00em; text-indent:-1.00em"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">&#149;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<B>Respect.</B> Treat customers,
suppliers, employees, and others with respect and courtesy.</FONT></P> <P STYLE="font-size:6px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px; margin-left:1.00em; text-indent:-1.00em"><FONT
FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">&#149;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<B>Confidentiality.</B> Protect the confidentiality of Apple&#146;s information and the information of our customers, suppliers, and employees.</FONT></P> <P
STYLE="font-size:6px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px; margin-left:1.00em; text-indent:-1.00em"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">&#149;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<B>Community.</B> Conduct business
in a way that benefits the communities in which we operate.</FONT></P> <P STYLE="font-size:6px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px; margin-left:1.00em; text-indent:-1.00em"><FONT
FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">&#149;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<B>Compliance.</B> Ensure that business decisions comply with all applicable laws and regulations.</FONT></P> <P STYLE="font-size:18px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="3">Making the Right Decisions</FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">When facing a tough decision:</FONT></P> <P
STYLE="font-size:6px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px; margin-left:1.00em; text-indent:-1.00em"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">&#149;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<B>Use good judgment.</B> Apply
Apple&#146;s principles of business conduct, review our policies, review legal requirements, and then decide what to do.</FONT></P> <P STYLE="font-size:6px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px; margin-left:1.00em; text-indent:-1.00em"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">&#149;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<B>Need some help?</B> When in doubt about how to proceed, discuss pending decisions with your manager,
your Human Resources representative, or the Legal Department. If you need more support, contact the Business Conduct Helpline.</FONT></P> <P STYLE="font-size:18px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="3">Your Responsibilities</FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:1px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Apple&#146;s business conduct policy and principles
apply to employees, independent contractors, consultants, and others who do business with Apple. All such individuals are expected to comply with Apple&#146;s business conduct policy and principles and with all applicable legal requirements. Apple
retains the right to discipline (up to and including termination of employment) or end working relationships with those who do not comply.</FONT></P></TD></TR>
</TABLE>

<TD VALIGN="top"> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="3">Customer Focus</FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:1px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Every product we make and every service

<TR>
<TD VALIGN="top"> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="1"><B>To what extent may I use an existing customer list to market other Apple products or services? </B></FONT></P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="1"><B></B>Before using a customer list for marketing, sales, or other activities, talk to your manager or the Legal Department. Using an existing customer list may or may
not be appropriate.<B></B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="font-size:12px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="font-size:12px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="font-size:12px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="1"><B>Where can I learn more about information protection and nondisclosure agreements?</B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT
FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="1"><B></B>View the Apple policy on Confidential, Proprietary, and Trade Secret Information.<B></B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="font-size:12px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="1"><B>Where can I get a nondisclosure agreement?</B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="1"><B></B>In the U.S., see the
forms Apple provides for nondisclosure agreements. Outside the U.S., consult your local legal team.<B></B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="font-size:12px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P> <P
STYLE="font-size:12px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="1"><B>Why is the source of business intelligence an issue, as long as the information helps Apple?</B>
</FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="1"><B></B>Obtaining information illegally or unethically could damage Apple&#146;s reputation and in some cases could subject Apple to legal liability. For
example, using illegally or unethically obtained information in a bid to the government could result in disqualification from future bidding and in criminal charges.<B></B></FONT></P> <P
STYLE="font-size:12px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="font-size:36px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="font-size:36px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P> <P
STYLE="font-size:12px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="font-size:6px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="1"><B>May I keep my personal music
on my computer at work? </B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:1px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="1"><B></B>If you are authorized to make copies of the music for personal use (for example, you own the original CD or you
purchased the music on iTunes), you may keep the music on your computer.<B></B></FONT></P></TD>
<TD VALIGN="bottom"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
<TD VALIGN="top"> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="3">Customer and Third-Party Information</FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Customers,
suppliers, and others disclose confidential information to Apple for business purposes. It is the responsibility of every Apple employee to protect and maintain the confidentiality of this information. Failure to protect customer and third-party
information may damage relations with customers, suppliers, or others and may result in legal liability. See the Apple Customer Privacy Policy.</FONT></P> <P STYLE="font-size:12px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="3">Nondisclosure Agreements</FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">When dealing with a supplier, vendor, or other third
party, never share confidential information without the approval of your manager. Also, never share confidential information outside Apple (for example, with vendors, suppliers, or others) unless a nondisclosure agreement is in place. These
agreements document the need to maintain the confidentiality of the information. Original copies of nondisclosure agreements must be forwarded to the Legal Department. Always limit the amount of confidential information shared to the minimum
necessary to address the business need.</FONT></P> <P STYLE="font-size:12px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="3">Obtaining and Using Business
Intelligence</FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Apple legitimately collects information on customers and markets in which we operate. Apple does not seek business intelligence by illegal or
unethical means, and competitors may not be contacted for the purpose of obtaining business intelligence. Sometimes information is obtained accidentally or is provided to Apple by unknown sources. In such cases, it may be unethical to use the
information, and you should immediately contact your manager, the Legal Department, or the Business Conduct Helpline to determine how to proceed.</FONT></P> <P STYLE="font-size:12px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="3">Third-Party Intellectual Property</FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">It is Apple&#146;s policy not to knowingly
use the intellectual property of any third party without permission or legal right. If you are told or suspect that Apple may be infringing an intellectual property right, including patents, copyrights, trademarks, or trade secrets owned by a third
party, you should contact the Legal Department.</FONT></P> <P STYLE="font-size:12px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="3">Copyright-Protected Content</FONT></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:1px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Never use or copy software, music, videos, publications, or other copyright-protected content at work or for business purposes unless you or Apple are legally
permitted to use or make copies of the protected content. Never use Apple facilities or equipment to make or store unauthorized copies.</FONT></P></TD></TR>
</TABLE>

<TD VALIGN="top"></TD>

<TD VALIGN="top"></TD>
<TD VALIGN="bottom"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
<TD VALIGN="top"> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="1"><B>Business Conduct</B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman"
SIZE="1"><B>The&nbsp;way&nbsp;we&nbsp;do&nbsp;business worldwide</B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:1px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="1">February 2009</FONT></P></TD>
<TD VALIGN="bottom"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
<TD VALIGN="top" ALIGN="center"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="1"><B>
 5
</B></FONT></TD></TR>
</TABLE> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></P>

<TABLE CELLSPACING="0" CELLPADDING="0" WIDTH="100%" BORDER="0" ALIGN="center">

<TR>
<TD WIDTH="29%"></TD>
<TD VALIGN="bottom" WIDTH="2%"></TD>
<TD WIDTH="69%"></TD></TR>
<TR>
<TD VALIGN="top"> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="1"><B>Are business meals, travel, and entertainment considered gifts?</B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT
FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="1"><B></B>Yes. Anything of value given or received is considered a gift.<B></B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="font-size:12px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT
FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="1"><B>Can I avoid these rules if I pay for gifts to customers or business associates myself?</B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="1"><B></B>No. If the gift is
given for business reasons and you are representing Apple, the gift rules apply.<B></B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="font-size:36px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="font-size:36px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P> <P
STYLE="font-size:36px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="font-size:36px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="font-size:36px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P> <P
STYLE="font-size:36px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="font-size:36px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="font-size:24px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P> <P
STYLE="font-size:12px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="1"><B>What is an example of a kickback?</B></FONT></P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="1"><B></B>Apple provides discounts to certain customers. However, if a customer gets an inappropriate discount, and a sales representative gets a payment in return, this is
a kickback.<B></B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="font-size:12px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="1"><B>What is an example of a side deal?</B></FONT></P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:1px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="1"><B></B>In a sales environment, a side deal may involve a guarantee to accept back unsold products or other special agreements to encourage certain customers to place
larger orders. Such a side deal, whether written or oral, can impact Apple&#146;s potential liability with respect to that transaction and may make it inappropriate for Apple to recognize revenue on the products sold, affecting the accuracy of
Apple&#146;s books and records. Side deals or side letters made outside of Apple&#146;s formal contracting and approvals process are prohibited.<B></B></FONT></P></TD>
<TD VALIGN="bottom"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
<TD VALIGN="top"> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="3">Giving and Receiving Business Gifts</FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Employees may not
give or receive gifts or entertainment to or from current or potential vendors, suppliers, customers, or other business associates unless all of the following conditions are met:</FONT></P> <P
STYLE="font-size:6px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px; margin-left:1.00em; text-indent:-1.00em"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">&#149;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<B>Nominal value.</B><B> </B>The
value of the gift is less than US$150. Exceptions must be approved by your Vice President (for Vice President&#150;level employees, exceptions must be approved by your manager).</FONT></P> <P
STYLE="font-size:6px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px; margin-left:1.00em; text-indent:-1.00em"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">&#149;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<B>Customary.</B> The item is a
customary business gift and would not embarrass Apple if publicly disclosed.</FONT></P> <P STYLE="font-size:6px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px; margin-left:1.00em; text-indent:-1.00em"><FONT
FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">&#149;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<B>No favored treatment.</B> The purpose of the gift is not to obtain special or favored treatment.</FONT></P> <P STYLE="font-size:6px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px; margin-left:1.00em; text-indent:-1.00em"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">&#149;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<B>Legal.</B> Giving or accepting the gift is legal in the location and under the circumstances where
given.</FONT></P> <P STYLE="font-size:6px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px; margin-left:1.00em; text-indent:-1.00em"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">&#149;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<B>Recipient is
not a government official.</B><B> </B>Never provide a gift, including meals, entertainment, and other items of value, to a U.S. or foreign government official without checking with Government Affairs in advance. See page 7 for more information on
gifts to government officials.</FONT></P> <P STYLE="font-size:12px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">This policy does not preclude Apple as an organization
from receiving and evaluating complimentary products or services. It is not intended to preclude Apple from giving equipment to a company or organization, provided the gift is openly given, consistent with legal requirements, and in Apple&#146;s
business interests. The policy also does not preclude the attendance of Apple employees at business-related social functions, if attendance is approved by management and does not create a conflict of interest.</FONT></P> <P
STYLE="font-size:18px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="3">Kickbacks</FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman"
SIZE="2">Kickbacks are payments or items of value given to individuals in connection with the purchase or sale of products or services, typically for providing a discount in a sales agreement. Employees are prohibited from giving or receiving
kickbacks.</FONT></P> <P STYLE="font-size:18px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="3">Side Deals or Side Letters</FONT></P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:1px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">All of the terms and conditions of agreements entered into by Apple must be formally documented. Contract terms and conditions define the key attributes of Apple&#146;s
rights, obligations, and liabilities and can also dictate the accounting treatment given to a transaction. Making business commitments outside of the formal contracting process, through side deals, &#147;side letters,&#148; or otherwise, is
unacceptable. You should not make any oral or written commitments that create a new agreement or modify an existing agreement without approval through the formal contracting process. In particular, all commitments must have visibility to Finance so
Apple can ensure it is properly accounting for each transaction. If you have knowledge of any side deal, side letter, or agreement made outside of the formal contracting process, you should report it immediately to your manager, your Human Resources
representative, or the Legal Department. You may also contact the Business Conduct Helpline.</FONT></P></TD></TR>
</TABLE>

<TR>
<TD VALIGN="top"> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="1"><B>What can I do if a reseller complains to me about low prices at another reseller?</B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT
FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="1"><B></B>Advise the reseller that you can&#146;t discuss or attempt to influence pricing of other parties, since this could violate antitrust laws.<B></B></FONT></P> <P
STYLE="font-size:252px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="1"><B>What is an example of an endorsement?</B></FONT></P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:1px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="1"><B></B>A friend writes a great book on software design and asks you to endorse the book by making a statement on the back cover. If you make such an endorsement,
don&#146;t include your job title or affiliation with Apple.<B></B></FONT></P></TD>
<TD VALIGN="bottom"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
<TD VALIGN="top"> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="3">Competition and Trade Practices</FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Laws regulating
competition and trade practices vary around the world, but certain activities, such as price fixing and agreeing with a competitor to allocate customers, are almost always illegal.</FONT></P> <P
STYLE="font-size:12px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">You should not:</FONT></P> <P STYLE="font-size:6px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px; margin-left:1.00em; text-indent:-1.00em"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">&#149;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Agree with competitors or exchange information with competitors on prices, policies, contract terms,
costs, inventories, marketing plans, or capacity plans.</FONT></P> <P STYLE="font-size:6px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px; margin-left:1.00em; text-indent:-1.00em"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman"
SIZE="2">&#149;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Agree with a competitor that the competitor will sell goods and services to Customer A (and you will not), and that you will sell goods and services to Customer B (and your competitor will not).</FONT></P> <P
STYLE="font-size:6px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px; margin-left:1.00em; text-indent:-1.00em"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">&#149;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Agree with resellers on the resale
pricing of Apple products without Legal Department approval.</FONT></P> <P STYLE="font-size:6px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px; margin-left:1.00em; text-indent:-1.00em"><FONT
FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">&#149;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Require vendors to purchase Apple products in order to sell products or services to Apple.</FONT></P> <P STYLE="font-size:6px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px; margin-left:1.00em; text-indent:-1.00em"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">&#149;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Describe the products or services of competitors inaccurately to promote Apple products or
services.</FONT></P> <P STYLE="font-size:6px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px; margin-left:1.00em; text-indent:-1.00em"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">&#149;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Engage in
any pricing or other practices that could defraud a supplier or others.</FONT></P> <P STYLE="font-size:6px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px; margin-left:1.00em; text-indent:-1.00em"><FONT
FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">&#149;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Violate fair bidding practices, including bidding quiet periods.</FONT></P> <P STYLE="font-size:18px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="3">Endorsements</FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">When representing Apple, never endorse a product or service of
another business or an individual, unless the endorsement has been approved by your manager. This does not apply to products of other businesses that are sold by Apple.</FONT></P> <P STYLE="font-size:18px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="3">Open Source Software</FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:1px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Open source software is software for which the source
code is available without charge under a free software or open source license. Before using or modifying any open source software for Apple infrastructure or as part of an Apple product or service development effort, you must a) review Apple&#146;s
Open Source Policy and b) contact the Legal Department for approval using the forms referenced in that Policy.</FONT></P></TD></TR>
</TABLE>

SIZE="1"><B>The&nbsp;way&nbsp;we&nbsp;do&nbsp;business worldwide</B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:1px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="1">February 2009</FONT></P></TD>

<TR>

<TD VALIGN="bottom" WIDTH="2%"></TD>
<TD WIDTH="69%"></TD></TR>
<TR>
<TD VALIGN="top"> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="1"><B>Tell me more about pricing products that are sold to U.S. and non-U.S. governments.</B></FONT></P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="1"><B></B>Governments shouldn&#146;t be charged more for our products or services than Apple charges other customers for the same products or services. There are laws that
make it a crime to overcharge the U.S. government. Some other countries have similar laws.<B></B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="font-size:48px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT
FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="1"><B>Can I avoid a gift limitation by paying for a gift, such as lunch or golf, myself?</B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="1"><B></B>No. If you are representing
Apple, any gift to a government employee would be viewed as coming from Apple.<B> </B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="font-size:12px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman"
SIZE="1"><B>What is considered a gift to a U.S. or foreign official?</B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="1"><B></B>In most cases, anything of value that is given is considered a gift. This
includes items such as meals, golf, entertainment, and product samples. Cash is never an acceptable gift. Typically, giving cash is viewed as a bribe or kickback and is against Apple policy.<B></B></FONT></P> <P
STYLE="font-size:12px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="1"><B>What is the difference between a facilitating payment and an illegal payment?</B></FONT></P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="1"><B></B>A facilitating payment is anything of value given to a foreign official for the purpose of expediting performance of certain routine, nondiscretionary activities.
An illegal payment is anything of value given to a foreign official for the purpose of obtaining or retaining business or to secure an improper advantage.<B></B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="font-size:12px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="1"><B>Who is considered a foreign official?</B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="1"><B></B>For purposes of the
Foreign Corrupt Practices Act, a &#147;foreign official&#148; is any official or employee of a foreign government, a public international organization (such as the European Commission), any department or agency thereof, or any person acting in an
official capacity. This could also include an official of a wholly or substantially state-owned business enterprise, such as a state-owned public utility.<B></B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="font-size:12px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P> <P
STYLE="font-size:12px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:1px">&nbsp;</P></TD>
<TD VALIGN="bottom"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
<TD VALIGN="top"> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="3">Governments as Customers</FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Governments are unique
customers for Apple. Governments often place special bidding, pricing, disclosure, and certification requirements on firms with which they do business. Discuss these requirements with the appropriate Apple attorney before bidding for government
business. For example, Apple may have to certify that it is supplying the government with the lowest price charged to Apple&#146;s commercial customers. Apple may also have to certify that its prices have been arrived at independently&#151;that is,
without collaboration with a third party.</FONT></P> <P STYLE="font-size:18px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="3">Gifts to U.S. Officials</FONT></P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">It may be illegal to give a gift, even an inexpensive meal or a T-shirt, to a government employee. The rules vary depending on the location of the employee (for example,
rules may vary by state, school district, and city) and the position held by the employee (for example, there may be different rules for various elected and nonelected officials).</FONT></P> <P
STYLE="font-size:12px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">To prevent violations, review planned gifts to government officials with Government Affairs in
advance of giving a gift.</FONT></P> <P STYLE="font-size:18px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="3">Gifts to Non-U.S. Officials</FONT></P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">In many countries it is considered common courtesy to provide token/ceremonial gifts to government officials on certain occasions to help build relationships. Check local
requirements and review any such gifts exceeding US$25 in advance with the Legal Department. For meals, the US$25 limit does not necessarily apply. Check here for value limits by country on meals to non-U.S. public officials and employees. Meals at
any value should be avoided with officials from government agencies where Apple has a pending application, proposal, or other business.</FONT></P> <P STYLE="font-size:12px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Offering or giving anything of value to a foreign official for the purpose of obtaining or retaining business or to secure any improper advantage is illegal. There is a
very limited exception for &#147;facilitating payments&#148; to foreign officials to expedite performance of routine activities such as obtaining permits or licenses; processing visas and work permits; or providing police, mail, or inspection
services. All facilitating payments must be preauthorized by the Legal Department and properly recorded and accounted for. Check with your manager or finance representative to determine the appropriate manner of reporting them.</FONT></P> <P
STYLE="font-size:12px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">For more information on the facilitating payments exception, see Apple&#146;s Foreign Corrupt
Practices Act Policy.</FONT></P> <P STYLE="font-size:18px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="3">Political Contributions</FONT></P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Apple contributes selectively to political candidates and committees. All corporate political contributions, whether monetary or in-kind (such as the donation/lending of
equipment or technical services to a campaign), must be approved in advance by Apple Government Affairs. Employees may not use Apple assets (including employee work time, or use of Apple premises, equipment, or funds) to personally support
candidates and campaigns.</FONT></P> <P STYLE="font-size:12px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:1px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">It is illegal for Apple to reimburse an employee for a
contribution. For more information, see the Apple Corporate Political Compliance Policy and the Political Contributions and Expenditures Policy.</FONT></P></TD></TR>
</TABLE>

<TD VALIGN="top"> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="1"><B>What if I&#146;d like to explore hiring a current government employee as a consultant?</B></FONT></P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="1"><B></B>Contact the Legal Department before beginning any negotiations.<B></B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="font-size:204px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P> <P
STYLE="font-size:12px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="1"><B>How do I get more information regarding Apple&#146;s environmental, health, and safety
programs?</B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="1"><B></B>Visit the Environment+Safety site.<B></B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="font-size:60px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="1"><B>What if I want to get more involved in community activities?</B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:1px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman"
SIZE="1"><B></B>Contact Community Affairs. This group promotes, supports, and facilitates employees&#146; involvement in community volunteer activities. Outside the U.S., check with your local Public Relations team.<B></B></FONT></P></TD>
<TD VALIGN="bottom"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
<TD VALIGN="top"> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="3">Hiring Government Employees</FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">U.S. laws limit the duties
and types of services that former U.S. government and military employees may perform as employees or consultants of Apple. In the U.S., employment negotiations with government employees are prohibited while the employees are participating in a
matter involving Apple&#146;s interests.</FONT></P> <P STYLE="font-size:18px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="3">Trade Restrictions and Export
Controls</FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Many countries periodically impose restrictions on exports and other dealings with certain other countries, persons, or groups. Export laws may
control trading of commodities or technologies that are considered to be strategically important because they have the potential to be used for military purposes. Laws may cover travel to or from a sanctioned country, imports or exports, new
investments, and other related topics. Certain laws also prohibit support of boycott activities. See Apple&#146;s Export Control policy for more information.</FONT></P> <P STYLE="font-size:12px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">If your work involves the sale or shipment of products, technologies, or services across international borders, check with the Export Department to ensure compliance with
any laws or restrictions that apply.</FONT></P> <P STYLE="font-size:18px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="3">Environment, Health, and Safety</FONT></P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Apple operates in a manner that conserves the environment and protects the safety and health of our employees. Conduct your job safely and consistent with applicable
environmental, health, and safety requirements. Use good judgment and always put the environment, safety, and health first. Be proactive in anticipating and dealing with environmental, health, and safety risks.</FONT></P> <P
STYLE="font-size:18px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="3">Community Activities</FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT
FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">At Apple, we comply with all laws and regulations and operate in ways that benefit the communities in which we conduct business. Apple encourages you to uphold this commitment to the community in all your activities.
</FONT></P> <P STYLE="font-size:12px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:1px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">If you hold an elected or appointed public office while employed at Apple, advise
Government Affairs. Excuse yourself from involvement in any decisions that might create or appear to create a conflict of interest.</FONT></P></TD></TR>

<TD VALIGN="bottom"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
<TD VALIGN="top"> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="1"><B>Business Conduct</B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman"
SIZE="1"><B>The&nbsp;way&nbsp;we&nbsp;do&nbsp;business worldwide</B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:1px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="1">February 2009</FONT></P></TD>

 9
</B></FONT></TD></TR>
</TABLE> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></P>

<TABLE CELLSPACING="0" CELLPADDING="0" WIDTH="100%" BORDER="0" ALIGN="center">

<TR>
<TD WIDTH="29%"></TD>
<TD VALIGN="bottom" WIDTH="2%"></TD>
<TD WIDTH="69%"></TD></TR>
<TR>
<TD VALIGN="top"> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="1"><B>What are assets?</B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="1"><B></B>Assets include
Apple&#146;s extremely valuable proprietary information (such as intellectual property, confidential business plans, unannounced product plans, sales and marketing strategies, and other trade secrets); as well as physical assets like cash,
equipment, supplies, and product inventory.<B></B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="font-size:12px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="1"><B>Where can I learn more about
information protection and nondisclosure agreements?</B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="1"><B></B>View the Apple policy on Confidential, Proprietary, and Trade Secret Information.<B></B>
</FONT></P> <P STYLE="font-size:132px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="font-size:36px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="1"><B>If I
believe that it is appropriate to disclose confidential proprietary information to a vendor or other third party, what should I do?</B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="1"><B></B>First, verify
that there is a business need for the disclosure. Second, obtain your manager&#146;s approval for the disclosure. Third, be sure that a nondisclosure agreement is in place with the vendor or third party, and that you forward the original copy of the
agreement to the Legal Department. If you are still unsure, check with the Legal Department before making the disclosure.<B></B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="font-size:36px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="1"><B>How do I identify confidential Apple information in documents?</B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman"
SIZE="1"><B></B>Mark these documents &#147;Apple Confidential.&#148;<B></B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="font-size:12px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="1"><B>What if
I have a specific question on the use of the Apple name, names of products or services, or the Apple logo?</B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="1"><B></B>Please direct questions about the
Apple corporate identity to corpID@apple.com.<B></B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="font-size:36px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="font-size:12px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="1"><B>How can I find out more about patents?</B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:1px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="1"><B></B>Visit Apple&#146;s
Patent Information site.<B></B></FONT></P></TD>
<TD VALIGN="bottom"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
<TD VALIGN="top"> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="3">Protecting Apple&#146;s Assets and Information</FONT></P> <P STYLE="font-size:6px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Protect Apple&#146;s assets:</FONT></P> <P STYLE="font-size:6px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px; margin-left:1.00em; text-indent:-1.00em"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">&#149;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;As an Apple employee you have a personal responsibility to protect Apple&#146;s property. You should
follow all security procedures, and be on the lookout for any instances you believe could lead to loss, misuse, or theft of company property. You should protect physical assets such as equipment, supplies, cash, and charge cards. And you should use
extreme care to protect from disclosure to any third parties Apple&#146;s proprietary information, including without limitation technical product information, information related to current and future products and services, confidential market
research, sales and marketing plans, nonpublic earnings or financial data, and organizational charts and information.</FONT></P> <P STYLE="font-size:6px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px; margin-left:1.00em; text-indent:-1.00em"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">&#149;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Follow procurement policies and procedures when acquiring goods or services on behalf of Apple, avoiding
any real or apparent conflict of interest. For more information on procurement policies and procedures, talk to your manager or visit Apple Procurement.</FONT></P> <P STYLE="font-size:6px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px; margin-left:1.00em; text-indent:-1.00em"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">&#149;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Use Apple&#146;s assets in a manner that prevents damage, waste, misuse, or theft. Use assets only for
legal and ethical purposes.</FONT></P> <P STYLE="font-size:6px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px; margin-left:1.00em; text-indent:-1.00em"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman"
SIZE="2">&#149;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Dispose of assets only with appropriate approval and in compliance with applicable policies. Before disposing of assets, discuss your plans with your manager.</FONT></P> <P
STYLE="font-size:18px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="3">Confidential Apple Information</FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT
FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">One of Apple&#146;s greatest assets is information about our products and services, including future product offerings. Never disclose confidential operational, financial, trade secret, or other business information
without verifying with your manager that such disclosure is appropriate. Typically, disclosure of this information is very limited, and the information may be shared with vendors, suppliers, or other third parties only after a nondisclosure
agreement is in place. Even within Apple, confidential information should be shared only on a need-to-know basis. The Intellectual Property Agreement you signed when you joined Apple defines your duty to protect information.</FONT></P> <P
STYLE="font-size:18px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="3">The Apple Identity and Trademarks</FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT
FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">The Apple name, names of products (such as iPod), names of services (such as AppleCare), tag lines (such as &#148;Don&#146;t steal music&#148;), and logos (such as the familiar Apple logo) collectively create the
Apple identity. Before publicly using the Apple name, product names, service names, tag lines, or the Apple logo, visit the Marketing site and select &#147;Corporate Identity&#148; for specific guidelines. Before using product names, service names,
tag lines, or logos of third parties, check with the Legal Department. Also keep in mind that there are corporate identity guidelines on how names and logos can be used and presented; for example, the size of the Apple logo and the amount of white
space surrounding the logo.</FONT></P> <P STYLE="font-size:18px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="3">Apple Inventions and Patents</FONT></P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:1px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Apple&#146;s practice is to consider for patenting the inventions of its employees, regardless of whether the inventions are implemented in actual products. If you are
involved in product development, you should contact the Legal Department regarding the patentability of your work. Be alert to possible infringement of Apple&#146;s patents and bring any possible infringements directly to the Legal
Department.</FONT></P></TD></TR>
</TABLE>

<TR>
<TD VALIGN="top"> <P STYLE="font-size:200px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="1"><B>How can I learn more about procedures for meals and travel?</B></FONT></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="1"><B></B>See Apple&#146;s Travel policy or talk to your manager.<B></B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="font-size:212px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="1"><B>If I suspect money laundering, what should I do?</B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:1px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="1"><B></B>Advise your
manager or contact the Apple Legal Department.<B></B></FONT></P></TD>
<TD VALIGN="bottom"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
<TD VALIGN="top"> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="3">Copyright Protection</FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">If you create original material for
Apple that requires copyright protection, such as software, place Apple&#146;s copyright notice on the work and submit a copyright disclosure form to the Legal Department. For more information, visit the Apple Copyright Information site.</FONT></P>
<P STYLE="font-size:18px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="3">Accuracy of Records and Reports</FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT
FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Accurate records are critical to meeting Apple&#146;s legal, financial, and management obligations. Ensure that all records and reports, including customer information, technical and product information,
correspondence, and public communications are full, fair, accurate, timely, and understandable.</FONT></P> <P STYLE="font-size:12px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman"
SIZE="2">Never misstate facts, omit critical information, or modify records or reports in any way to mislead others, or assist others in doing so.</FONT></P> <P STYLE="font-size:18px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="3">Business Expenses</FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">All employees must observe policies and procedures
regarding business expenses, such as meal and travel expenses, and submit accurate expense reimbursement requests. Guidelines on daily meal expenses vary worldwide.</FONT></P> <P STYLE="font-size:18px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="3">Establishing Bank Accounts</FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">All Apple bank accounts must be approved and
established by Apple&#146;s Treasury Department. All payments must be made by recordable and traceable methods. For more information, contact the Treasury Department.</FONT></P> <P STYLE="font-size:18px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="3">Loans, Advances, and Guarantees</FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Other than through established corporate
programs, such as programs for employee relocation and the cashless exercise of stock options, Apple does not provide loans or advances of corporate funds to its employees, officers, Board members, or their families and does not guarantee their
obligations.</FONT></P> <P STYLE="font-size:18px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="3">Money Laundering</FONT></P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Money laundering is the process by which individuals or organizations try to conceal illicit funds or make these funds look legitimate. If you are in a position to deal
directly with customers or vendors, the following examples may be indications of potential money laundering:</FONT></P> <P STYLE="font-size:6px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px; margin-left:1.00em; text-indent:-1.00em"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">&#149;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Attempts to make large payments in cash</FONT></P> <P
STYLE="font-size:6px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px; margin-left:1.00em; text-indent:-1.00em"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">&#149;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Payments by someone who is not a
party to the contract</FONT></P> <P STYLE="font-size:6px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px; margin-left:1.00em; text-indent:-1.00em"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman"
SIZE="2">&#149;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Requests to pay more than provided for in the contract</FONT></P> <P STYLE="font-size:6px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px; margin-left:1.00em; text-indent:-1.00em"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">&#149;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Payments made in currencies other than those specified in the contract</FONT></P> <P
STYLE="font-size:6px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:1px; margin-left:1.00em; text-indent:-1.00em"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">&#149;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Payments from an unusual,
nonbusiness account</FONT></P></TD></TR>
</TABLE>

<TD VALIGN="bottom"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></TD>

<TD VALIGN="top"></TD>
<TD VALIGN="bottom"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
<TD VALIGN="top"> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="1"><B>Business Conduct</B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman"
SIZE="1"><B>The&nbsp;way&nbsp;we&nbsp;do&nbsp;business worldwide</B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:1px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="1">February 2009</FONT></P></TD>

<TABLE CELLSPACING="0" CELLPADDING="0" WIDTH="100%" BORDER="0" ALIGN="center">

<TR>
<TD WIDTH="29%"></TD>
<TD VALIGN="bottom" WIDTH="2%"></TD>
<TD WIDTH="69%"></TD></TR>
<TR>
<TD VALIGN="top"> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="1"><B>Tell me more about &#147;legal holds.&#148;</B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:1px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman"
SIZE="1"><B></B>In a litigation case or other legal matter, Apple may be required to produce documents. In these cases the Legal Department may put a &#147;legal hold&#148; on certain documents to prevent the documents from being destroyed, altered,
or modified. If it is found that Apple has failed to retain or produce required documents, penalties or adverse rulings may result. Adverse rulings in major litigation cases can cost Apple a significant amount of money. Failure of employees to
retain and preserve documents placed on a legal hold may result in discipline or discharge.<B></B></FONT></P></TD>
<TD VALIGN="bottom"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
<TD VALIGN="top"> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="3">Document Retention and Legal Hold</FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">As an Apple employee,
you have a responsibility to manage documents and make decisions on document retention. The definition of &#147;document&#148; is extremely broad. For example, every email or other electronic file, every customer record, and every transaction
involves the creation of a document. Different documents have different retention periods. Check with your manager or contact Records Management to determine the appropriate retention period for documents in your area.</FONT></P> <P
STYLE="font-size:12px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:1px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">At times, Apple may need to retain documents beyond the period they would normally be retained. The
most common reasons are litigation or other legal matters. In these situations, retention and preservation of documents is critical. If you have documents that may be required for litigation or other legal matters, the Legal Department will place
those documents on a &#147;legal hold,&#148; meaning the documents cannot be altered, destroyed, deleted, or modified in any manner, and will inform the individuals most closely identified with the documents. Instructions for retaining the documents
will be provided, and you must ensure that these instructions are followed. A legal hold remains in effect until you are notified by the Legal Department in writing.</FONT></P></TD></TR>
</TABLE>

<TD VALIGN="top"> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="1"><B>Business Conduct</B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman"
SIZE="1"><B>The&nbsp;way&nbsp;we&nbsp;do&nbsp;business worldwide</B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:1px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="1">February 2009</FONT></P></TD>

 12
</B></FONT></TD></TR>
</TABLE> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></P>

<TABLE CELLSPACING="0" CELLPADDING="0" WIDTH="100%" BORDER="0" ALIGN="center">

<TR>
<TD WIDTH="29%"></TD>
<TD VALIGN="bottom" WIDTH="2%"></TD>
<TD WIDTH="69%"></TD></TR>
<TR>
<TD VALIGN="top"> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="1"><B>Can you give an example of conflicts of interest or potential divided loyalty?</B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT
FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="1"><B></B>Your brother-in-law owns a business, that business is being considered as a vendor for Apple, and you are one of the decision makers.<B></B></FONT></P> <P
STYLE="font-size:48px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="font-size:6px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="1"><B>May I occasionally use my
Apple email address for my outside business?</B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="1"><B></B>Limited personal use of your Apple email is permitted for activities such as sending a brief message
to a friend. You may never use your Apple email for an outside business.<B></B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="font-size:12px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman"
SIZE="1"><B>I&#146;m working on an invention on my own time. Does Apple need to know?</B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="1"><B></B>If your invention relates to your job at Apple or could
compete with current or reasonably anticipated future products or services of Apple, disclose the invention to your manager.<B></B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="font-size:12px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="1"><B>May I serve on the board of directors of an outside enterprise or organization?</B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman"
SIZE="1"><B></B>If you plan to serve on a board, you must obtain approval from your manager and the Senior Vice President for your organization. In addition, Vice Presidents and Executive Team members must obtain the approval of their manager and
the CEO before they can accept a position on the board of directors of a private or publicly traded company (other than nonprofit entities).<B></B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="font-size:96px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P> <P
STYLE="font-size:24px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="1"><B>What does &#147;significant personal relationship&#148; mean?</B></FONT></P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:1px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="1"><B></B>Significant personal relationships include close friends and relatives and may even include a long-term acquaintance or neighbor. If you are unsure, the best
approach is to disclose the potential conflict to your manager.<B></B></FONT></P></TD>
<TD VALIGN="bottom"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
<TD VALIGN="top"> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="3">Conflicts of Interest</FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">A conflict of interest is any
activity that is inconsistent with or opposed to Apple&#146;s best interests, or that gives the appearance of impropriety or divided loyalty. Avoid any situation that creates a real or perceived conflict of interest. Use good judgment, and if you
are unsure about a potential conflict, talk to your manager, contact Human Resources, check with the Legal Department, or contact the Business Conduct Helpline.</FONT></P> <P STYLE="font-size:18px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="3">Outside Employment and Inventions</FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">If you are a full-time Apple employee,
taking any other employment, full-time or part-time, requires that you notify your manager. In addition, any employee (full-time or part-time) who obtains outside employment (such as a part-time job away from Apple), has an outside business, or is
working on an invention must comply with the following rules.</FONT></P> <P STYLE="font-size:12px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Do not:</FONT></P> <P
STYLE="font-size:6px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px; margin-left:1.00em; text-indent:-1.00em"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">&#149;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Use any time at work or any Apple
assets for your other job, outside business, or invention. This includes using Apple workspace, telephones, computers, Internet access, copy machines, and any other Apple assets or services.</FONT></P> <P
STYLE="font-size:6px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px; margin-left:1.00em; text-indent:-1.00em"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">&#149;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Use your position at Apple to
solicit work for your outside business or other employer, to obtain favored treatment, or to pressure others to assist you in working on your invention.</FONT></P> <P STYLE="font-size:6px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px; margin-left:1.00em; text-indent:-1.00em"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">&#149;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Use confidential Apple information to benefit your other employer, outside business, or
invention.</FONT></P> <P STYLE="font-size:6px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px; margin-left:1.00em; text-indent:-1.00em"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">&#149;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Participate
in an outside employment activity that could have an adverse effect on your ability to perform your duties at Apple.</FONT></P> <P STYLE="font-size:6px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px; margin-left:1.00em; text-indent:-1.00em"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">&#149;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Participate in an outside business or outside employment, or develop an invention, that is in an area of
Apple&#146;s present or reasonably anticipated future business.</FONT></P> <P STYLE="font-size:12px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Before participating
in inventions or businesses that are in the same area as your work for Apple or that compete with or relate to present or reasonably anticipated Apple products or services, you must have written permission from your manager, an Apple product law
attorney, and the Senior Vice President of your organization. View Apple&#146;s policy on Conflicts of Interest.</FONT></P> <P STYLE="font-size:18px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT
FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="3">Significant Personal Relationships</FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Do not conduct Apple business with family members or others with whom you have a
significant personal relationship. In rare cases where exceptions may be appropriate, written approval from the Senior Vice President for your organization is required.</FONT></P> <P STYLE="font-size:12px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:1px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">You shouldn&#146;t use your position at Apple to obtain favored treatment for yourself, family members, or others with whom you have a significant relationship. This
applies to product purchases or sales, investment opportunities, hiring, promoting, selecting contractors or suppliers, and any other business matter. This does not apply to special purchase plans offered by Apple. If you believe you have a
potential conflict involving a family member or other individual, disclose it to your manager.</FONT></P></TD></TR>
</TABLE>

<TD VALIGN="bottom"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
